The 5-story building walls are postensioned with CCL Scandinavia's C-system to withstand the 
lateral forces. The thickness of the walls is determined based on the geometry of the anchoring. 
Common anchor dimensions used in Denmark are used.
The buildings with 5-8 stories are considered. The prestressing lines are adapted for each building. The 
verification is as follows:
1) Check turnover of walls.
2) Check compression zone.
3) Check sliding.

Concrete Core - Reinforcement and Shear Capacity
Verification for max. vertical loading and cracks are not considered. The anchoring and prestressed tendons are 
not considered in the following. The 4-story and 8-story building walls are considered, since these represents 
the remaining walls.

==PAGE:299==
Load Distribution between Fasteners in Shear Connection
In the following, the load distribution between the fasteners in the vertical 
shear connection is investigated using FEM approach and manual 
calculation.
Manual calculation
Vertical shear connections
Basically, the external force is distributed to the inner fasteners through equilibrium in the load direction, and 
the moment from eccentricity is taken by the outermost fasteners.
Examples of load distribution in fasteners [Timber connections, 11353 guest lecture. JГёrgen Munch-
Andersen. 2020]
According to the load distribution in the figure, it is favorable to have only one stacked column of fasteners.
To utilize the fasteners as much as possible, the ratio between the capacity per connection, 
, to the 
Rv.d.con
number of fasteners per connection per meter, 
, should approach, but not exceed, the shear flow, 
nf.con
.
nxy
This means, that there should be as few fasteners as possible, and they should have as high capacity as 
possible.
A plastic force distribution between the fasteners is investigated parametrically, to get an initial idea about the 
force distribution in a connection. It is then assumed, that the two outermost fasteners take the moment, and the 
remaining fasteners take the shear.
Sum of fastener forces can calculated by:

вҖҘ

3
4
The force distribution follows elasticity, but a plastic distribution is often used when doing a manual 
calculation.
The two outermost fasteners can be modelled to only take up the moment, by modelling them as horizontal 
supports only. The remaining fasteners are modelled as vertical supports. The model with 2 fasteners is not 
included in this analysis.
The FE-model distributes the load elastically between the vertical supports, 
depending on the rigidity of the modelled steel plate. As can be seen, the max. 
vertical reactions therefore occur in the outermost vertical supports.

[kN]

The results yield the same horizontal resultants no matter the number of fasteners. This seems to be in 
agreement with what was found in the manual analysis.
The vertical resultants decline with number of fasteners.
Comparing with the previous analysis, the horizontal reactions are larger, the vertical reactions are larger, and 
the max. reactions are larger than the resulting reactions in the previous analysis. It is therefore safe to use the 
distribution.
To compare with the manually calculated results, the sum of the reaction forces are estimated.

Stiffness of plate
The effect of the stiffness of the plate is in Eurocode included in the slip modulus by material only. Supports

thicknesses,

significantly.

None of the compressive stresses exceed 
.
fc.x.d
More stresses will need to be verified in further analyses. The column reduction factor is not used in this check, 
since column buckling will occur in the middle of a floor, and not at the support. The compressive stresses are 
spread out over the compression zone, and could be larger, if only the area of the peak stress was considered.
It is noted, that the contact stress in the left panel approaches the contact stress in the right panel for lower 
values of 
due to coupling behavior (this will not be investigated further here).

Stress distribution on deformed wall base

Determination of minimum capacity of shear connection
The 5-story building is considered. A stiffness of the joint in SLS of 35 kN/mm per meter has been settled. 
Since a higher stiffness will attract more forces, the stiffness is set higher to 85 kN/mm per meter, in order 
to estimate a conservative shear flow (the value has been determined in later investigations of shear 
connection).  A rigid model with a rigid connection is used as a reference.
The the mesh has been refined to an average element size of 0.1m
35 вҖ•вҖ•
kN
mm
m

85 вҖ•вҖ•
kN

-1
Rigid
35 вҖ•вҖ•

-1
85 вҖ•вҖ•
kN
mm
m
-1
Rigid
Shear flow [kN/m] between panels for different 
stiffnesses with a linear calculation 
Shear flow [kN/m] between panels for different 
stiffnesses with a non-linear uplift calculation 
The rigid model provides the largest shear flow, since it attracts the most forces. It is included in the analysis 
to see, what the max. obtainable shear flow is. The highest shear flow value for the model with stiffness of 85 
kN/mm per meter is adapted. The large increases in shear flow near the supports are ignored. The value is 
rounded up to the nearest natural number.

Kinematic behavior of wall
prEN 1995-1-1 suggests different definitions of kinematic modes of a wall, which depends on geometry and, 
load conditions and stiffnesses; see figure below. The definitions are only valid for shear walls in platform-
frame construction, and not for balloon-frame construction, where the latter is the case for this project. The 
following investigation is therefore only meant as a reference, and is not conclusive. 
Rocking kinematic modes for a segmented CLT shear wall acc. to prEN 1995-1-1
The kinematic modes are conditioned by the following.

Minimum distances
Minimum distances for fasteners are established to avoid splitting of the timber. Two sources for minimum 
fastener distances are considered. Rothoblaas provides minimum distances the SBD, which should be based 
on Eurocode 5 for dowels, though it differs on the unloaded edge distance 
. [CLT] provides minimum 
a4.t
distances for dowels in CLT-structures, which also should be based on Eurocode.

For multiple shear plane connections, the capacity is calculated by considering each shear plane as a part of a

of failure modes, where the the failure modes with rope-effect cannot be combined.

Strength
The shear capacity acc. to the Johansen yield theory is calculated below. For dowels, the rope effect is not 
allowed to be utilized acc. to DS/EN 1995. The four-shear-plane connection is considered as a series of two 
double-shear-plane connections, and the failure modes are a combination of the compatible failure modes for 
the two double-shear-plane connections.
Failure modes for double-shear plane connections [JMA22]
Acc. to [JMA22], failure mode C should be aimed for, by having the outer members thinner than the inner 
members, which maximizes resistance and ductility of the connection. Failure mode E, G, and F should be 
avoided,

Reduced cross-section
The reduced cross-section of the CLT has to carry the 
shear forces. The effective thickness of the nodes between 
the layers are calculated as the minimum of two times the 
outer layer thickness or the inner layer thickness.

The required thicknesses are far too large for the CLT, and is therefore not followed. They could be reduced by 
using smaller dowels, since the desired ductile failure modes are characterized by multiple plastic hinges in the 
fasteners.
Placement of steel plates
Failure mode (C) or (D) should be aimed for. It will now be investigated where the steel plates shall be placed, 
for a ductile failure mode to be obtained.

Strength
The shear capacity acc. to the Johansen yield theory is calculated below. For dowels, the rope effect is not 
allowed to be utilized acc. to DS/EN 1995. The four-shear-plane connection is considered as a series of two 
double-shear-plane connections, and the failure modes are a combination of the compatible failure modes for 
the two double-shear-plane connections.

Shear buckling
Shear buckling is investigated in acc. with DS/EN 1993-1-5 from equations by Henning Agerskov April 2009 
"Buckling of plates (initial buckling)".
The method is for plates with line supports, why it is a simplification. The plate is technically supported by the 
dowels, why it is hard to do a standardized verification.
The plate will also be held in place by the CLT, why it is on the safe side to do the check.

Optimization of Connection
It shall be investigated, if failure mode (C) can be obtained by changing the thickness of the steel plates and 
the diameters of the dowels. All other previously determined parameters are the same.

Failure mode B vs steel plate thickness with M12 STA dowel
It can be seen, that failure mode (C) is governing until it crosses with failure mode (F). The max. steel plate 
thickness can thereby be found, for failure mode (C) to be obtained. Failure mode (B) is governing until it 
crosses failure mode (C). The min. thickness can thereby also be found.
